<div id="review_621698186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621698186" />
    <a title="Winston Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17709230-winston-jen"><img alt="Winston Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563549289p2/17709230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621698186?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Winston Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Winston Jen" href="/user/show/17709230-winston-jen">Winston Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17709230-winston-jen?shelf=self-harm">self-harm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17709230-winston-jen?shelf=apologetics">apologetics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621698186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer613465914260072944">Strobel simply cannot think critically when it comes to his religion. He demonstrates this in another of his books, "The Case for Christ," which I suppose is used to draw us to Christianity over Islam, Hindiusm or Buddhism. In a nutshell, Strobel brings forth New Testament historians. Wow. Why bring people with a vested interest and a well-established opinion to talk about historical figures? But I've digressed, onto the<br/><br/>1. Strobel interviews Peter Kreeft about the Problem of Evil/Suffering: Spec</span>
  <span id="freeText613465914260072944" style="display:none">Strobel simply cannot think critically when it comes to his religion. He demonstrates this in another of his books, "The Case for Christ," which I suppose is used to draw us to Christianity over Islam, Hindiusm or Buddhism. In a nutshell, Strobel brings forth New Testament historians. Wow. Why bring people with a vested interest and a well-established opinion to talk about historical figures? But I've digressed, onto the<br /><br />1. Strobel interviews Peter Kreeft about the Problem of Evil/Suffering: Special pleading and little else. A tri-omni god (all-loving, all-knowing and all-powerful) would not allow any suffering to occur. Any so-called "greater good" can be accomplished without using ANY suffering. Therefore, the existence of ANY suffering demolishes the possibility of such a god existing.<br /><br />2. Since Miracles Contradict Science, They Cannot Be True: Special pleading, and circular to boot. Strobel and Craig use miracles to prove a deity. They have it precisely in reverse; please prove your god first and THEN use him to prove miracles (and while you're at it, please show why there have been fewer miracle claims in the past 200 years. For that matter, why do events such as finding one's car keys qualify as miracles today?)<br /><br />3. Evolution Explains Life, So God Isn't Needed: this isn't really an issue; there are millions of theistic evolutionists in the world. But in any case, evolution and abiogenesis are completely separate theories. By conflating the two, Bradley is being dishonest. In any case, abiogenesis has been proven by modern science. No god required here. Just watch any online "debate" on evolution and Christianity to see how weak Creationist arguments are.<br /><br />4. God Isn't Worthy of Worship If He Kills Innocent Children: A perfect god would not need to use mass slaughter as a first OR a last resort. The genocides in the old testament were perpetrated by humans. God's edicts were created on an ad hoc basis to justify child slaughter. And in any case, wouldn't sending children to heaven be a wondrous act of compassion and altruism, under Christian doctrine?<br /><br />5. It's Offensive to Claim Jesus Is the Only Way to God: First you have to prove god without using circular arguments, Mr. Strobel. Try again later.<br /><br />6. A Loving God Would Never Torture People in Hell: Wow. So hell is a "mercy" according to Strobel JP Moreland. Hell is for those who do not wish to spend eternity with their god. Wow.<br /><br />7. Church History is Littered with Oppression &amp; Violence: Strobel again dodges the issue; a tri-omni god would not have allowed any suffering to occur. The Problem of Suffering is invincible against such a being.<br /><br />And the red herrings brought up () Next!<br /><br />8. I Still Have Doubts, So I Can't Be a Christian: "Trust us!" That is Lee's closing requiem for his book. And given the previous seven chapters, I cannot trust someone of his caliber.<br /><br />Avoid this book at all costs. Unless you want to be the life of a skeptic's party.</span>
  <a data-text-id="613465914260072944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_526082167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/526082167" />
    <a title="Patricia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16135710-patricia"><img alt="Patricia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360195176p2/16135710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/526082167?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricia" href="/user/show/16135710-patricia">Patricia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Christians and Jesus Seekers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer526082167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4362542989840824478">In _the case for faith_, Strobel attempts to tackle the top 8 criticisms or objections to forging a Christian faith. He interviews eight scholars, who each hold prestigious appointments at reputable tier 1 to 3 schools, and have authored numerous publications--though many are through Christian presses. Each scholar is meant to be the credible voice on one of the eight objections.<br/><br/>Strobel employs a formulaic writing style, such that his chapters read rather similarly. The structure he uses: 1) beg</span>
  <span id="freeText4362542989840824478" style="display:none">In _the case for faith_, Strobel attempts to tackle the top 8 criticisms or objections to forging a Christian faith. He interviews eight scholars, who each hold prestigious appointments at reputable tier 1 to 3 schools, and have authored numerous publications--though many are through Christian presses. Each scholar is meant to be the credible voice on one of the eight objections.<br /><br />Strobel employs a formulaic writing style, such that his chapters read rather similarly. The structure he uses: 1) begin the chapter with an anecdote that introduces the objection in an emotionally charged and socially relevant way; 2) proclaim that "[strobel] needed to find someone who could tackle this dilemma head-on!"; 3) introduce the interviewee, his appearance and home or office, and his credentials (all male); 4) explain that Strobel wouldn't make things easy for the interviewee, which apparently bolsters Strobel's ethos 5) provide a prose transcript of the interview, which is meant to dismantle many of the objections and any related sub-points. <br /><br />I appreciated the formulaic approach, since I could focus on the content more than Strobel's style. As for tackling the toughest criticisms of a Christian faith, much was left unhandled. For example, Strobel interviews someone on the objection, "why does God let children suffer?" (I cannot recall the exact title of the chapter). The interviewee only tackled two scenarios of children's suffering, but didn't explore other examples of suffering, e.g. Mental limitations and physical deformities. On the other hand, Strobel's interviews often provide answers that are quite compelling and explanatory. For instance, a chapter is devoted to the question of why God, who hates when his children suffer, would send people to hell when he wouldn't necessarily have to. The interviewee explains that what makes hell terrible is that it is void of God. The suffering comes from regretting the choice to remain the center of your universe rather than making God the center. To the scholar, our time on earth is an incubation period wherein we each decide if we want to be with God or not. We have free will, so we get to decide on hell or heaven. <br /><br />That explanation might sound ridiculous to many people, but it gave a satisfying answer to the enduring question of "what is life for?" The answer, according to this text, is that it's meant for us to identify if we want eternity with or without God. That's a pretty decent answer, I'd say.<br /><br />Of course, the book cannot begin to absolutely sell the sceptic on Christianity. There are many omissions, and necessarily so: a book can only be so long! But if you're a seeker or you are looking to reinforce your Christian faith, Strobel's texts are for you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4362542989840824478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VOiTBuX40zatMATRGjHUvCozbuzn0OZfWW4vFursTq3xr0QjiBTo84XgsC/gfFVL1EYb89hOvQBgZ5JCrZUaMg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+ONFnDnBlyyVMa5p56riCCQ5XC7IZSj4rfAV8w1RjxZdpJK5VC2s6b3hGpcd52P/2kwpMff7c6eU+ainSijbiQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4790094585128637891">Lee Patrick Strobel is an American Christian author, journalist, apologist and pastor. He has written several books, including four which received ECPA Christian Book Awards (1994, 1999, 2001, 2005) and a series which addresses challenges to a Biblically inerrant view of Christianity. Strobel also hosted a television program called Faith Under Fire on PAX TV, and runs a video apologetics web site.</span>
  <span id="freeText4790094585128637891" style="display:none">Lee Patrick Strobel is an American Christian author, journalist, apologist and pastor. He has written several books, including four which received ECPA Christian Book Awards (1994, 1999, 2001, 2005) and a series which addresses challenges to a Biblically inerrant view of Christianity. Strobel also hosted a television program called Faith Under Fire on PAX TV, and runs a video apologetics web site. Strobel has been interviewed on numerous national television programs, including ABC's 20/20, Fox News, and CNN.</span>
